<Review>As a Midwesterner who is newly  moved here, mountains are a novelty and I love seeing them where I live. After hearing about the 5 Peak Challenge at Mission Trails Regional Park, I knew this was the challenge I needed since races in person are canceled for the time being.
The parking lot filled up quickly as noted but I easily parked on the road outside the lot. The path to the summit was busy for 8am, but everyone was moving at a easy pace and enjoying the gorgeous weather. There are parts of the path where you have to climb over rocks but overall it isn‚Äôt too bad. For the websites that said this is a great hike for kids, I say, what age, because this was a killer workout for me but to be fair, I come from straight flat land! Beautiful views at the peak. 5<//Rate>
<Text>This is a great hike with great views at the summit. There are several approaches to the summit. From the Santee side which is a little more challenging and from a couple San Diego neighborhoods. At night you have great views of the city lights, in the day a great view of Lake Murray and the mountains to the south and east. It is also a great place to catch a sunrise or a sunset. Like always be in good enough physical condition, bring water, and wear proper clothing. Dogs are allowed on a leash. Be sure to have water for them as well.< /Text><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMkyjdlclqtqarpkdT4JMr4FAY8dHmE3f7C5-NM=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNo5yN20BX1KT4c9YZF8CGMmsmpnf1Ns5tFOANm=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMlxl_1iBUuhTQ9PvOclNCID6aYUG0gqjzzCPd9=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>< response>

<GmapID>0x80d957cb5c163f3d:0x14922199dd16ce0d<//GmapID><UserId.>109853612072177883971< /UserId.><time>1561661864617<//time></record>
</dataset><record>
< Text>
Cowles Mountain is the go-to hike in the City of San Diego. It's easy to get to from the 125 freeway off Navajo. Parking at busy times can be a real nightmare. Don't be surprised if you have to park 1/4 mile away and walk to the trailhead. But you're out for a good hike anyway, so what's an extra 1000 feet to you? Because the trail is popular, there does tend to be a lot of people on-site. If you are a fast hiker, you will likely get stuck behind some slower folks, but there are plenty of opportunities to pass them. The main trail is NOT open to bicycles, but you can ride a mountain bike up the eastern entrance / fire road that is available off of Barker Way. Cowles is popular for all ages and most abilities. There are a few spots where the rocks are steep, but don't let it be intimidating. Most of the trail is basic and smooth, with the occasion step(s) up. Often you will see the more athletic types RUNNING up and down the mountain. The round trip is about 50-120 minutes depending on your abilities. The view from the top is fantastic, which is part of why Cowles Mountain is so popular. Give it a shot today (or tonight... as many hikers take their flashlights to enjoy a night hike.)< /Text>

How could I not give 5 star. The view is worth the hike. You keep walking and wonder when you will actually be getting there and just when you think you're at the top, you got 20 min more to go.
Anyways, I was bright enough to go hiking with a glass water bottle (who does that?) and on my way back down as I told myself.. after skidding just a bit on one corner that this was probably not a good idea (the glass), the next corner I took I ended up slipping on some dry dirt and smashed to the floor: it was like slow motion for me. < review>
8/6/19

I decided to rewrite my review for this nail salon because although at times humor is definitely the best medicine to cheer yourself up after‚Ä¶it‚Äôs not the best way to show you that you should stay away from this place at all costs.

I went in with my mother and we both wanted pedicures. After a few minutes of waiting, we finally got a seat at the massage chairs. My mother and I both got male ‚Äúnail techs‚Äù or whatever they want to pass themselves off as.

I was sitting and the man handed me a laminated paper with the different pedicure packages and their prices. I decided to go with the package that has the basics and only the callus remover which was supposed to be $30. So, I told the man that was what I wanted. The time before I came, I got a gel pedicure, so the man noticed and tried to convince me not once, not twice‚Ä¶not three times but FOUR times for me to get gel and blah blah blah. I totally get how upselling works, but if a customer says no‚Äîmultiple times. It means no. To add, because he knew I had gel previously, he bumped up my price $5 more to remove my gel polish??? I‚Äôm sorry‚Ä¶what? So if that weren‚Äôt frustrating enough, the man who was working on my toes decided to bump down my package to the basics but instead of the callus remover, he did the paraffin wax. As someone who is working at a place‚Ä¶it is NOT your place to downgrade your paying customer to something they didn‚Äôt originally ask for. This new package was going to cost $28.

So he begins using cotton pads to remove the gel off of my toes, and he maybe let the solution on the pads sit for about 30 seconds. Then he took off the pads from my toes and began aggressively filing off the polish from my toes with so much force. For time sake, I am going to put the actual part that made me literally scream.

The nail tech goes to the back and brings back the hot towels and the paraffin wax. He then he proceeds to grab the paraffin wax bags and doesn't even feel it, but by the way he was handling the bags, I had a feeling the wax was VERY hot. And he stuck my foot in there and it was indeed WAY too hot. I told him multiple times that it was very hot and clearly from my sudden reaction and repetition, everyone around me saw my reaction and saw that this was no laughing matter. He proceeded to press in the paraffin wax to form my foot. What upset me beyond belief was the fact that this man literally told me, ‚ÄúNo it‚Äôs not hot‚Ä¶.no it no burn‚Ä¶‚Äù Are you kidding me?? Are you really trying to ignore my blatant cries and tell me that you did not just burn me??? By this point, I was very very close to tears. I don't even think he was able to handle the heat from the plastic bags because he turned on the cool water and pushed my foot down forcefully in there. After about a couple of minutes, he proceeded to put my right foot into a different bag with wax. This one was manageable unlike the first time. After some time passed, he came back and took the bags off of my feet and all of the toes on my left foot were very pink and were in so much pain. He began aggressively massaging that specific foot because he too, must have saw how horribly pinkish red they were. I felt my toes becoming almost numb and hot. ***** I also have attached a picture of both of my feet, where you can visibly see my left toes were burnt and inflamed. *******

It truly disgusts me that this man tried to tell me otherwise that he did not burn me. My point is, nail techs need to understand that they are not working on wax figures or whatever, these are real people that they are working on and they can cause real damage to their customers. I will never be stepping foot at this nail salon again.</review>

When the process began, I closed my eyes and felt was the hot wax applied first to my right eyebrow. As soon as she tore off the first strip from my eyebrow, I just felt a painful burn sensation, but thought it was normal due to the sensitivity previously mentioned.   I noticed that she stopped a few minutes to get cotton and start wiping my eye with some kind of liquid.  I noticed that she did wipe several times then continued on.   After she was done waxing my right eyebrow, she suggested that I get my eyebrows waxed several days prior to my event so that my make-up will blend better with my eyebrows.
